Accordingly, the patient sometimes claims she is a stone that Christ saves or to which Professor

A Case of Schizophrenia  29 Forel, a “sculptural artist of the psyche,” gives colors of life.

In addition, the patient often lies there without moving and claims to be crucified.

Jesus Christ saves me through the pure air of his earth, or vice versa.

The air becomes water, and the earth becomes a woman.

It is the Protestant and Catholic insanity which needs to be dissolved in a pure way.

The patient became insane.

She is a Protestant, the husband a Catholic.

For that reason, the insanity (used in the sense of conflict) is a Protestant and a Catholic one.

The patient (the woman) is saved through the air of Jesus.

The air is the spirit (the intellect, psychical), and the earth (woman) is the body (the physical).

The air turns into water; that is, the spiritual turns into the physical. “The earth becomes a woman.”24 The woman (patient) is saved through the (holy) water of Jesus.

The patient’s subsequent remarks belong in the same realm of religious symbolism: I saw Forel in the death chamber on J (Ward for the Restless).

He has an organ of his own characterized by clarity and truth of the water.

The water has to be blessed and is blessed by him.

The water becomes bread, and the bread is blessed by him.

In Professor Forel’s alcohol question, I saw that the sons will bury their father alive.

Yet, someone who is buried alive will become a vineyard, and the wine will turn into blood.

This is the significance of the Last Supper.

Professor Forel has committed an act of abuse for which he must atone.

His land has been cultivated by a curse.

Why, in this case, the sons bury their father, I do not know.

Perhaps one has to understand it in this way: The father must die in order for the sons to be born, since, as we know, the sons are created from the father.

We also heard the remark, “In order to create a new generation, the whole body needs to be prepared.”25 Bleuler brought to my attention respective Greek myths (Kronos and Zeus).

The patient is dead.

For that reason, her chamber (cell) is a death chamber.

When the living Professor Forel enters it, he is buried alive.

However, he who is buried alive returns to the world in a new form, in the form of a wine-producing vine, respectively, since wine = sperm, in the form of a sperm-producing sexual organism.

30  A Case of Schizophrenia Question: “How does the water become bread?” Answer: “The water is saturated with childlikeness, because God asks us to become like children.

There is also spermatic water that can be saturated with blood.

Perhaps that is the water of Jesus.

The water of the man, just as the water of the woman, must have a pure earth.” I only asked the question so that the patient would express what I had already sufficiently understood: For everyone knows that one receives in the wine (to the patient “the spermatic water of Jesus, saturated with blood”), and in the bread, the blood and the body of Jesus.

The bread turns into the body.

Of course, the body (bread) that is made from the (spermatic) water is the child.

The patient explicitly mentions this: “The water is saturated with childlikeness.” She confirms this by saying, “Become like the children,” that is, become children, or rather, “I become my own child.” The water (of Professor Forel) needs to have a pure earth, but the patient is not pure, she is land that has been worked on by a curse. 26  A full understanding of this religious-psychological material could only be achieved through appropriate historical research.

However, for the most part, this has not yet been conducted. 27  3.

Histology and its treatment The patient perceives “histology” as an illness, namely an illness of the tissue.

Histology is the teaching about tissue or the science of the tissue.

The scholars upon whom the patient focuses are all doctors, and she, the patient, and, more specifically, her illness, are the object of their research (their science); for this reason, science itself is called illness.

In addition, the patient distinguishes a “psychological histology,” by which she means “the decrease of love, a kind of fear of people which has to do with melancholy.” “Histology is based on the connection of melancholy with sexual diseases or women’s diseases,” the patient says. “Perhaps it is a paraphrase for the events during menstruation and the purification that is associated with them, in other words, with the women’s question regarding female period; the latter represents physical histology.” Thus we see that by “tissues,” the tissue of the female genitals is meant.

Furthermore, the term “histology” is shifted, by no longer only denoting a disease of the tissue, but also the melancholy associated with it.

The sentence, “It is a paraphrase for menstruation processes,” is in its

A Case of Schizophrenia  31 form reminiscent of the following sentence in the previous chapter: “It is a description of the Italian lakes.” Birth was described there in the following way: The amniotic fluid that comes out of the female genitals was represented in the form of lakes that emerge from a crevice in the earth (= woman).

Instead of saying, “It is the birth,” the patient says, “It is a description.” The same happens here: Instead of saying, the disease of the tissue (histology) is an anomaly in the menstruation process or rather, consists of an anomaly of the menstruation process, the patient uses less specific words: “It is a paraphrase.” She uses the expression, “periodic women’s question” [Frauenfrage], instead of calling it the period in women.

The significance of “period” = purification hardly needs to be explained.

The assumption that the female period purifies the blood is widespread.

In men, the patient distinguishes a “spermatic purification.” Let us further listen to the patient: Professor Forel was interested in the creation of breast milk.

The mother has to nourish her children herself.

Not every mother can afford a wet nurse.

My children were fed artificial milk.

The calcium in the milk creates horrible burning in the female genitals that can only be alleviated by the male member that religion has created out of need: by spermatic cure.

Here the patient blames herself for having to feed her children artificial milk.

She had to do this due to an illness that consisted of horrible burning pain in her genitals.

This illness can only be cured (saved) by coitus.

The man with whom she wants to have intercourse is Professor Forel.

If he cures her, then she herself will have milk to feed her children (“Professor Forel was interested in the creation of breast milk.”) The voices accuse her of having “impure desires with Professor Forel.”28 The lowliness of the Catholic Church creates a physical pain in me that I feel in my blood.

The pain can be alleviated by psychological purification.

Purgatory, idealism, Dante, Jesus Christ saves me through the pure air of his earth.

As we have learned, air becomes the spermatic water.

The earth is the body which yields this water so that the patient’s flight into the psychological realm leads her into the physical realm, as it usually does.

Furthermore, she reports:

32  A Case of Schizophrenia Spermatic cure takes place when medicine (the doctor) provides pure health.

When medicine gives something impure, a disease develops, perhaps an infection with syphilis that leads to insanity, degeneration, and limpness of the body.

My husband probably had syphilis.

I noticed this on the discharges of his spermatic purification.

One has to prevent this in children.

There was a healthy generation of Alemannic people who created the family . . .

My husband contracted syphilis while being unfaithful.

We just saw that the patient seeks a cure in coitus.

However, she wants to have intercourse with a “pure” man from whom she could have a child (create a family).

The “medicine” of her husband, whom she found sexually repulsive, could only make her ill.

At the same time, she thinks about saving the children.

She continues: The actual act has something quite dirty about it, if I were indeed a person who masturbates, but I am not.

My children are not allowed to do it because it makes one ill.

It was not me who wet the bed; it was a different manipulative woman.

It is interesting that the patient, much earlier, had mentioned rebukes for bed-wetting.

When I informed Professor Bleuler about this, he said it might have to do with the masturbation complex.

I refrained from asking the patient about it, to ensure that I avoided suggestion.

Now it turns out that Professor Bleuler’s assumption was correct.

The patient indicates that, as a small child, “perhaps” she wet her bed.

She continues: When children wet their bed, it means their bladder is recovering from a cold or from hitting.

Lime water can cause such infections in children.

I was told of a variety of seeds, natural products, which could help in such a case.

In this comment, the bladder that caught a cold (is ill) represents the sexual organ.

Lime water has the same meaning as the above-mentioned lime milk.

The therapy is also the same (through “a variety of seeds”).

Yet it is only alluded to in a rather obscure way.

Furthermore, we learn, “I had to give an enema to my little boy for three months” (constipation due

A Case of Schizophrenia  33 to masturbation, as she later indicates). “I myself had obstruction of the esophagus and bowels” (also due to masturbation) “that resulted from a ruined nervous system.

It happened because of my husband.” At this point, she admits that she used to masturbate as a child, and she adds: It has to do with the later histology: When the sexual nerves become limp, then a woman can no longer suffice in a marriage.

Genetics is something dirty and impure, but it creates disgust for masturbation.

This has to do with the making of an angel.

The patient had a stillbirth.

This is what the “making of an angel” means, for which she blames masturbation. “Catholic religion involves rawness of the senses.

If it is only physical duty, not love, it is a sacrifice . . .

I was infected with syphilis.” We can see that the rebukes that the patient hears are not without reason.

She really masturbated and, because of this, had obstruction of the esophagus and bowels (as she later claims); so did her little son.

Therefore, in her eyes, masturbation must be blamed for her insufficiency (illness), her coldness towards her husband, and the birth of a dead child.

On the other hand, her husband’s rawness of senses (the Catholic religion), and his sexual excesses were the reason for her coldness towards him and why she had to masturbate.

If she loved her husband, then she would not masturbate.

In this light, the treatment of having intercourse with a “pure” man for whom the patient longs seems to make sense.

The patient continues: “That Woman (her husband’s female student) became jealous and threw herself on me with her revolting body, with her knees; she vented her cruelest anger on me.” Frequently, the patient hears voices ordering her to hit That Woman.

Hitting seems to have a sexual meaning for the patient.

Let us recall that she derived the bladder infection from “a cold it caught or from hitting.” The seemingly capricious juxtaposition of such different causes can be explained in that the cold [of the bladder] = coldness, and lack of love, just as hitting = rough treatment, represents the merely animalistic component of the sexual drive.

As a child, the patient was seduced to masturbate at a Vehmic Trial game during carnival season.

We learned about the nature of this Vehmic Trial in chapter 2.

On this occasion, she is “judged” by Dr. J.

He expels “the crudeness of the wine” (therefore, of her husband) out of her by treating her in an

34  A Case of Schizophrenia equally brutal and animalistic way as does her husband.

She is “beaten through Basel.” Immediately thereafter procreation fantasies occur. 29  Besides the hitting, we have, as further clues, the sexual aggression of the patient towards That Woman, and vice versa.

For example, she claims That Woman had given her pure saliva and urine to drink.

Let us recall how the earth is contaminated by receiving urine together with semen. 30  The patient then elaborates: “The woman bribed my children to masturbate on her.

We would have never been asked to do this on our mother.” (Here she suddenly imagines hearing the voices of her children.) “That Woman ordered the children to stick their fingers in her sexual organ and to derive pleasure from her through masturbation.” Question: “What is the name of That Woman?” Answer: “She has adopted my name, X.” The patient expresses her identification with “That Woman,” not only by having sexual relations with her, but also by having the same name as she.

In this way, “That Woman,” whom she hates, takes the place of the patient, and she becomes a symbol for all impulses that are “revolting” to her consciousness and, therefore, represents her sexual personality.

Her mother and children with whom she has sexual relations, too, become the same symbols.

We will hear more about this in a moment.

The medical history states that the patient could not eat anything for a rather long time after her little child had swallowed a small ball.

It reminded her of the obstruction of the esophagus.

When her mother fell ill with cancer (in colloquial language, obstruction of the esophagus), the patient experienced fits of choking and believed she was going to die, like her mother. “Masturbation leads to obstruction of the bowels and the esophagus,”31 she explained to me.

Thus she perceived the incidents with the child and her mother as a phenomenon that was caused by masturbation.

By doing this, she projects her own sexual identity onto her mother and her child, who become symbols for her.

On the other hand, by way of identification, she herself becomes her own mother and, respectively, her own child, and experiences the fate of both.

She also mentioned that it seemed to her that the nature and character of her mother had been transferred to her and that her mother was treating her like a child. “That Woman” had “slandered” her in front of her mother, so that her mother accused her of bed-wetting,

A Case of Schizophrenia  35 just as she wanted to accuse her little son of this.

Thus again, the patient is, on one hand, the mother, and on the other hand, she assumes the position of a child.

Why is this so?

Her fantasy that she becomes a “little Forel” provides us with the explanation, for we know that the patient projected her love onto Dr. J. = Professor Forel.

From that, by the same mechanism as described by Schreber,32 “a little Forel” is created.

Schreber’s projection onto Flechsig left in him a “little Flechsig.” She herself, however, becomes a little Forel. 33  For that reason, her identification with the child also means that she expects a child from Forel.

As a mother, the patient experiences the same fate as her own mother.

Her mother was operated on by Professor Kocher in Bern.

The patient mistakes him for [Robert] Koch, “who developed the vaccine therapy [Tuberculin] against tuberculosis.” The patient needs to receive the same treatment that her mother underwent and, therefore, must suffer from tuberculosis, which she does by claiming that she suffers from lung disease and syphilis.

The way in which she processes her mother’s illness is evidenced by the fact that she combines syphilis with tuberculosis which, in her eyes, equals sexual excessiveness.

It is also shown by the following. “The son of the Kocher family, a surgeon in Bern, is my fiercest opponent.

He wanted to force me to enjoy pleasure in sex.” Since sexual diseases are cured by the sexual act, we comprehend Kocher’s treatment.

However, why “the son”?

Let us listen to what she says next: “Kocher’s brother . . . the physical fights which provoke irritations, until one loses one’s temper; he himself does not hit, but orders others to do so.” Here she imagines hearing the voice of a man, “He incites the female guards to hit her.” “This is not a way to treat tuberculosis!” Question: “What is his name?” Answer: “Hans must be his name.” Question: “Who is Hans?” Answer: “My boy’s name is also Hans.

He claims he can get away with it because he is Professor Koch’s son.

He wants to provoke something in order to get control over me.” We are not surprised that, instead of Professor Koch, his brother appears.

In the last example as well, instead of Professor Forel, his brother – Dr. J. – appeared. 34  This substitution shows that Professor Koch is clearly an equivalent to Professor Forel.

Therefore, we may assume that the two

36  A Case of Schizophrenia brothers as well represent the same person.

By not hitting her himself, but by ordering others to hit her, Professor Koch gains greater authority, in the same way as when a judge pronounces a verdict, but others have to administer the punishment.

Dr. J. does not hit her himself either, but she is “beaten through Basel.” Her favorite son Hans and Professor Kocher’s son play the same role.

The latter is also given the name “Hans.” Furthermore, the patient says with an expression of utmost surprise: “Hans must be his name!?” and remembers that her child’s name, too, is Hans.

This identification of the two children makes Professor Kocher the patient’s “husband.” What we hear from the patient in the following confirms this assumption: Marmite is the lymph.

Why don’t you consult Kocher’s chemistry?

It has to do with tuberculosis.

Professor Kocher himself is an alcoholic for the purpose of examination.

The alcohol needs to be thinned down with coffee and bread, so it can go through the fistula and out with the faeces, the alcohol mixed with mineral water and coffee, and milk with pure bread.

Question: “Marmite, as we know, in German means ‘pan.’” Answer: “Yes, it is the Kocher pan, the cooking pot of chemistry!” We know that humans are created “through chemistry.” The pan in which the process takes place would, therefore, again be the uterus. 35  The word “cooking pot,” instead of “pan,” is a mediating association between Kocher [related to kochen = to cook] and cooking.

Like Dr. J., Professor Koch is an “alcoholic for the purpose of examination.” Like Dr. J., he first needs to examine and then “perform the function that is connected with the Sistine (sexual) question.”36 As we have seen earlier, alcohol – sperm, bread – represent the childlikeness dissolved in spermatic water; therefore, the child.

The “fistula” through which the child comes out is, of course, the opening of the vagina.

But why with the faeces?

In the next chapter, we will find more proof that in her fantasies, the patient treats the digestive tract as a sexual organ.

Adding milk to the alcohol (sperm) is necessary because the patient suffers from lack of breast milk production. 37  By coffee, probably blood is meant because its brown color is reminiscent of coagulated blood (?).

Right after this follow associations that are about blood and strongly stress its red color.

A Case of Schizophrenia  37 “Controlling alcohol,” the patient says, “has to happen by a new supply of blood, by cooking red beetroots in red wine, by boiling them down to syrup, and by using the rest of the medication again for cooking purposes.” Here the word “alcohol” is used in a broader sense, as sexual misbehavior and excess.

Sexual excessiveness is also controlled by coitus.

The following are considered remedies: renewed “supply of blood,” “root,”38 “wine” (= alcohol = “the spermatic blood-soaked water of Jesus”).

All these remedies are red like the dominant feature of “blood.” However, the word “cooking” raises questions.

It is, at first, an allusion to Professor Kocher.

Furthermore, cooking means heating up something by using fire.

We have already learned the meaning of fire as an all-purifying agent.

From all of this one may conclude that boiling, just like burning, is a sexual act that happens in “fiery” love. 39  In order to fight sexual dysentery, a new supply of blood, a new formation of substances is required.

I want to contact Professor Forel.

The psychological therapeutics could be explained through Laocoön’s genesis and refined through Scott’s emulsion.

As one might expect, she mentions Professor Forel and then the psychological therapeutics, that is, Dr. J.’s association experiment.

Furthermore, she states: People with a histological illness (= people who have a tissue illness), should not be provoked.

I don’t want to cook for the husband but for children.

That would mean the psychological pan that does not bestow hate, but peace.

We just discussed that cooking refers to the sexual act which the patient wants to experience with the children. “Psychological” (the asexual) suggests a protest against the sexual (for the psychological pan is contrasted with the animalistic one). “Psychological therapeutics,” of course, need a psychological pan, just as the psychological coitus needs an animalistic pan.

To where does this opposition to the animalistic lead?

Let us recall that the water (Jesus) “is saturated with childlikeness,” because Jesus says: “Become like the children.” We already know that in the patient’s thinking, “to become a child” means “to bear a child.”40

38  A Case of Schizophrenia Here, too, the patient wants to become innocent “like a child,” by cooking for the children or, based on what we already know, by identifying herself with the children through sexual relations.

This identification, as discussed earlier, means that she becomes her own child, or rather gives birth to a child.

Let us summarize what we have examined in this chapter: We have seen that certain symptoms of illness ostensibly were linked to random experiences.

To the patient, there was always a logical connection between the symptom and the etiological event.

As was explained earlier, the patient constantly makes strong self-recriminations for masturbating.

She blames this vice for each mishap, for her coldness towards her husband and for his unfaithfulness, and for her spontaneous abortion.

She constantly thinks of masturbation and, therefore, is reminded of masturbation by every more or less appropriate event imaginable.

This happens in practically every strong complex. 41  However, a normal person will look at the obtrusive analogies and comparisons as just that, whereas the patient does not distinguish whether something is only similar or is identical. 42  The obstruction of the larynx by a small ball in the child and, in the case of the mother, the obstruction of the esophagus due to cancer, remind the patient of the obstruction of the bowels (that is, the obstipation resulting from masturbation).

In her mother and in her child, she now sees herself, and solely herself.

Furthermore, by looking at what these persons desire and how they act, we see that their needs and desires are all those of the patient and primarily in relation to herself.

In this way, the mother, the child, and others, for example That Woman, serve as symbols to her.

As another consequence of this identification, the patient uses situations in her family for the formation of her symbols, to which she assigns her own meaning, namely in terms of wish fulfillment of the unsatisfied complex which strives for permanent power over the psyche as a whole. 43  Stekel, in “Contributions to the Interpretation of Dreams,”44 claims that relatives in a dream represent the genitals.

In essence, this seems to be true, except, instead of using the term “genitals,” I would use “sexual personality,” because it would be a broader term.

One could apply the same explanation also to the dreams of normal people, where relatives become vehicles of the dreamer’s desires.

It is also likely that most of the repressed wishes are, in a narrower or broader sense, of a sexual nature.

The patient, in her

A Case of Schizophrenia  39 imagination, has a decisively sexual relationship to her children.

This might partially be the result of an immediate sexual affinity, since each strong love has a slight sexual coloring.

However, in the dream, inhibitions that exist during the day disappear,45 so that the sexual component emerges more clearly.

One loves a person insofar as one sees a similarity in that person.

The most perfected identification is the sexual union, which is also the climax of sexual activity. 46  We have encountered this process in the identification with the children and That Woman.

The latter is the object of hate in the patient’s consciousness (rejection of love).

However, the children too are partially the symbols that represent the patient’s desires or wishes which she forces upon those persons for whom she is longing.

Thus we encounter, for example, “Hans” instead of his father Professor Kocher.

Equally, we see how her own children assume her (the patient’s) role.

The children, who all have her ailments, masturbate, for example, also with That Woman with whom the patient claims to have had a sexual encounter.

In short, the children represent “sexual personalities.” In this chapter, we also explore the notion of illness as a complex, as a sexual disease caused by masturbation, or rather, coitus.

The treatment should consist of a sexual act with a healthy man.

It is interesting that the patient does not always use terms in the same sense.

For example, by “histology” she means at times illness of the tissue, other times the melancholy associated with it.

By “Marmite” she mostly means “pan,” but once also “lymph.” She only adheres to a general category, but sometimes changes details.

Now and again, one gains the impression that she is struggling for the right forms of expression, that is, for symbols. “She tries to confuse you,” the doctor treating her told me.

She turns all possible, even slightly related, things into symbols of the same thought, just like in a dream.

We can observe this best in the next chapter. 4.

The industrial or economic question We had the opportunity to observe in the patient allusions to the poverty complex.

She complained to us that her husband preferred a richer and more beautiful girl over her.

Shaped by her poverty complex, her procreation fantasies focus on the growth of “blessed money.” During the

40  A Case of Schizophrenia first analysis, she mentioned: “The stitchery comes in contact with prostitution in order to earn money.” It has become apparent that she calls herself “stitchery” because she had to earn money by doing stitchery.

She often also calls herself “a prostitute.” Moreover, she frequently uses “to stitch” [sticken], instead of “to suffocate” [ersticken], for the dislocation of the larynx, the esophagus, and the intestines as a result of masturbation.

Therefore, stitchery is also synonymous with “woman masturbator.” The patient does not attempt to differentiate between the two terms. 47  Both have the same underlying cause, the lack of money, which forces her, on one hand, to earn money, on the other hand, to masturbate because of the resulting lack of love.

The following comments of the patient fit into this context: The disinfection of the bowels would be necessary for the children and for me.

In my case, it was the lack of treatment for an illness, syphilis and tuberculosis.

It is the logic of the poor.

The doctors ought to assert themselves in such a situation and say: Either you will be killed, or you will be buried alive in a coffin, if you reject the disinfection.

If the poor don’t want the disinfection, they must endure punishment by Jesus Christ.

The disinfection has to do with the soap question.

One has to do the soap disinfection with pungent acids, possibly mixed with mitigating agents.

The bowels are disinfected by these agents which are taken with the agent, with the bread.

Professor Forel worked on this.

We hear again of diseases that, as we know, signify bad sexual behavior.

The patient mentions “soap disinfection” as a means of treatment.

From what we have learned so far about this kind of treatment, we can assume that the means of treatment above is again the “spermatic water” and, therefore, we can expect to encounter “alcohol,” “substances of Kocher’s chemistry,” etc., and other similar associations, and we do: Like alcohol, which “cleanses everything,” disinfecting is also a means of cleansing.

Like alcohol, or rather the Kocher substances, it is taken with the bread.

As in that case, here too, the bread corresponds to the “childlikeness” (= the child), which is dissolved in the water.

The term itself, “soap question,” already points to the “alcoholic” Forel and his Sexual Question and, finally, the patient explicitly claims the following: “Professor Forel has worked on it (that is, on the agent).” The sperm

A Case of Schizophrenia  41 symbol has the function of disinfecting the bowels.

This suggests that the patient uses the digestive tract in the sense of genitals.

Syphilis and tuberculosis must be cured through coitus with a healthy man (the doctor).

If she were rich, she could do herself this favor.

However, since she is poor, she has untreated illnesses, and the doctors have “to insist on disinfection.” At the same time, the patient wants the poor to be killed, to be buried alive,48 and punished by Jesus Christ.

This seems to be a contradiction in her treatment of the poor.

However, I believe it only appears to be one.

The punishment (Vehmic Trial), killing, etc., equally represent the sexual act, as we have seen earlier, only this time the component of being overpowered predominates.

In Adler’s opinion, this self-incriminating component is a necessary compensation for “sin.” The idea of soap disinfection is probably taken from reality, since the patient was likely disinfected during the obstetric operations.

However, the disinfection was assigned a different meaning that corresponds to her complex.

Following the disinfection question, the patient said something about her children which, unfortunately, I could not write down since she said it so fast.

She then continues: The industrial or metaphysical question must have to do with the nutrition question.

Here the dissolution of combustible materials [Verbrennungsstoffe], through ingestion of food, serves the development of substances in the body.

If, for example, one burns parts of spoiled objects, even if they are metallic, geological or vegetarian products of the earth, with existing substances and adds the ashes to the food with a disinfecting liquid, it must be considered an economic-metaphysical experiment of the question of human dust development with regard to psychic influences that could be of a cheerful or funny nature.

The “Sexual Question” (Forel) seems to give continuous shape to all the patient’s “questions,” since time and again, another “question” arises.

The nutrition question is an industrial question inasmuch as the workers, with whom the patient identifies, have to eat.

At the same time, for the patient, eating means “sexually enjoying.”49 The patient is ill and impure.

Therefore she is an impure earth (woman) and, accordingly, produces spoiled objects, that is, metals with regards to fuels (as we will later see,

42  A Case of Schizophrenia elements for life in the form of alcohol). “Iron can fortify the body,” she says, “since one also uses the term of an iron constitution.” Furthermore, the earth produces geological objects.

(Let us recall the stone symbolism!) Finally, we also have “vegetarian” products. “Vegetarian” again signifies a major rejection, or rather, the affirmation of the animalistic. 50  These products of the woman (earth) have to be burned with other (healthy) products, or according to our previous analysis, come together in love (fire!).

Instead of these products joining together in the woman’s body, the act in her case is fragmented due to her strong defence against everything sexual which she perceives as dirty.

A “disinfecting liquid” is added to the materials that have been burnt to ashes, before they are added to the food.

When looking at the soap disinfection we learned that the disinfectant corresponds to sperm.

Thus we find the first sexual act in the burning to ashes51 and the second in the treatment with a disinfecting liquid, so that the negation has become, at the very least, a double affirmation.

Let’s again listen to the patient: Disinfection of parts of spoiled objects, perhaps by cleansing with soda.

Ingestion of food for the development of elements in the body, for example, broken pieces of porcelain, a silk band that is no longer worth the trouble to be washed, silk fabric, lace with a dried piece of porcelain.

If a piece of gold or silver is cleansed, washed, burnt, alcoholized [alkoholisiert], and dried again, and its ashes are used as a powder in a dish, then these lead to observations about the brain function.

Observations of mercury and gold lead to the economic question of the renewed formation of materials and also to the psychology of the development of the parts of these materials.

Question: “Into what do these material components develop?” Answer: “Well, it depends on whether they are good or bad influences, explanations, dream interpretations.

It would be a kind of potash development for the purification of the Physe [body].

This powder could also be boiled, so it does not create dangerous symptoms, for example, blockages, blockages of the cells, and Vehmic blockages.” Let us first examine how the different materials are processed: They are purified.

The word purifying is probably stressed four times, since

A Case of Schizophrenia  43 “washed” equals the word “purified.” Furthermore, as we have learned, alcohol and fire purify everything. “Purification,” as we know, is to the patient a sexual event; that is, coitus.

The objects are being “dried.” We can understand the word “drying” if we recall that the earth is contaminated by urine and, furthermore, if we recollect the respective accusations with regard to “bed-wetting” on the part of That Woman.

Not only this patient, but many others as well, perceive bed-wetting as masturbation.

The connection can be found in the close proximity of micturition and the sexual act on one hand, and insuccation of the aroused vulva on the other hand.

She stressed twice that for this form of wetting (that is, for masturbation), “drying” is required.

The purified and dried objects produce the ashes.

In chapter 2, “Psychological-Sistine experiments,” we have already learned about the burning to ashes.

There the patient explicitly stated: “Ash can become a human being.” Here again, the burning (= sterilizing by boiling) is emphasized. “This powder (first called ‘ashes,’ then ‘potash’52) could be boiled, so it does not cause dangerous symptoms, for example blockages, blockages of the cells, Vehmic blockages.” The abbreviated form “blockages” is repeated and modified until it is called “Vehmic blockages.” For she tells us that, as a child, while playing a game at a Vehmic Trial, she was seduced to masturbate.

Masturbation causes constipation, as we have already heard from her, therefore the contraction “Vehmic blockage.” As the reason for masturbating, the patient mentions the coldness she feels towards her husband.

Now we understand that the ashes (that is, the sexual product), need to be boiled or – which is the same – that coitus has to happen in “hot” love, for if it merely “is physical obligation,” if one is not in love (is cold), one lapses into masturbation which causes “blockages.” We have now reached the question about into what the materials develop. “The first results are observations of the brain function,” says the patient. “Looking,” “examining,” and “observing” are the same as, correspondingly, “performing the function in order to test the experiments.”53 For that reason, one also observes “brain functions” (which are at the same time the opposite of the animalistic and an allusion to Dr. J.’s association experiment).

The result of the development of the substances depends on whether it concerned a good or a bad person; it “depends on whether the

44  A Case of Schizophrenia influences, interpretations, and dream explanations were good or bad” (= “psychological” treatment).

The “potash” is the product of the psychological treatment and serves “the purification of the body.” As previously mentioned, the patient is evasive.

Instead of saying what happens to the ash (= sexual product), she explains what one should do with it by clinging to the idea of sterilization by boiling (= sexual act).

Which materials are used for the creation of the “powder” (ash)?

Mostly, they are damaged objects, such as the broken porcelain, and the silk ribbon “that is no longer worth the trouble to wash.” I cannot determine what the patient is trying to express by porcelain. 54  We learned that she became a stone to which Professor Forel gave colors of life.

In the following passage, we will encounter a young male painter who does the same by painting on stones.

The artist’s mother, supposedly, loves painted porcelain.

Thus it is possible that porcelain means the same as stone and, in particular, that broken porcelain represents the patient’s broken soul.

The patient uses silk and laces as expressions of wealth: “The poor cannot wear garments with laces,” she says. “They also have to make do with more simple silk.” Therefore, the obsolete silk band represents the destroyed wealth.

To these objects that the poor (thus the patient) provide, objects of the rich are added, such as silk fabric, laces, gold, and silver.

Silver already occurred as a link to a different group of ideas to which mercury belongs; that is, to the illness of syphilis, which is the result of a life in luxury and is treated with mercury.

In addition to her observations about the brain functions, the patient talks about observations concerning mercury and gold, which represent, in this case, the detrimental consequences of wealth. 55  These belong to the “economic question,” which, as we know, ought to deal with the “treatment” of the poor.

Short summary: The patient takes various objects of poverty and wealth and makes them join in love like sexual beings, or rather sexual objects; that is, she makes them copulate.

The result is ash, the product of love (burning) from which, as we have heard earlier, new humans are created.

In order to understand what follows, we must recall that in 1903, the patient had experienced a spontaneous abortion.

In her medical history, we find fantasies about a stone child to whom she had given birth in a dream while suffering pain.

The female director supposedly said it was going to be an animal.

Furthermore, in the institution, the patient hallucinated about a corpse coming back from the dead and also “children in glass coffins

A Case of Schizophrenia  45 smashed to pieces.” After her mother’s cremation, she took a few bone fragments home.

Let us listen to what the patient says next: The powder one could use for the economic treatment of scrofula following the question of dysentery, after the glass purification.

In order to purify the bones, broken glass is boiled and strained.

In order to do this, one has to take vegetarian powder, for example, peeled and grated apples.

That is the question of digestion.

This powder is taken with coffee or soup.

After her spontaneous abortion, the patient had hallucinations about children in glass coffins.

What does the glass coffin stand for?

The patient connects the “cleaning of the glass” with the “dysentery question.” We encountered the question of sexual “dysentery” in the beginning of chapter 2, “Psychological-Sistine experiments.” There we heard about the three pans, of which the “vegetarian one” meant contempt for the flesh (rejection of sexuality).

The pan turned out to mean uterus, just like its analogy, “the cooking pot of chemistry.” We also heard about vegetarian fruit powder that turned out to be sperm.

We have heard already many times that sexual dysentery is treated with “purification,” and have noticed that “purification” equals impregnation.

Furthermore, the patient complains about the untreated “tuberculosis” among the poor, against which the doctors should use “disinfection” (= impregnation).

Here she talks about the “economic” treatment of scrofula.

The word “economic” points to the connection with the “economic” question; that is, the question of the poor.

Scrofula corresponds to tuberculosis.

Therefore, the statement says “treatment of tuberculosis among the poor.” First, the glass needs to be “purified,” which corresponds to the “purification” of the bowels (used for uterus, as we earlier showed).

As before, here, too, sperm is used for “purification.” Our assumption is corroborated when we hear about the “vegetarian powder,” since “vegetarian,” as we have always noticed, represents something quite animalistic.

Thus the glass coffin is the uterus which is impregnated.

We will understand from the following why the uterus is also boiled and, only afterwards, crushed.

Novozoon (= sperm) is extracted “from the head and the spermatic development in the animal.” “In order to create the new generation, the whole body needs to be preserved.” “Novozoon” is a “dead substance.” Therefore, the living organism needs to be killed, ground, and

46  A Case of Schizophrenia dissolved for the purpose of procreation.

On the other hand, killing, etc., also has the meaning of saving and bringing to life.

Why are the bones cleaned?

Bones belong mostly to the realm of the dead person who can be brought back to life through “spermatic treatment.” However, the patient has another idea that explains how bones become unclean objects: “The stitching and the metaphysical bone calcification come from the Vehmic blockage.” “Vehmic blockage” is, as we know, the result of masturbation.

Masturbation is the cause for sexual diseases that, in turn, lead to a lack of breast milk. “Artificial milk contains a lot of calcium.” In this way, the calcification of the bones is the result of Vehmic blockage, or rather of masturbation.

Masturbation, as well as the bones that were “soiled” (calcified) by it, must be treated with “purification.” The calcification is called “metaphysical.” “Metaphysics,” according to the patient, means “overpowering.” “If one has too much iron in one’s body,” she explains, “one becomes overpowering, for people say ‘iron constitution.’ The reason for the excessive amount of iron is related to the consumption of alcohol.” According to the patient, if one consumes alcohol, one develops too much power due to the iron.

We will later see that “iron” is more or less synonymous with “alcohol.” The patient claims that her husband was an alcoholic.

In the beginning, alcohol increases libido (probably that was one of the reasons why she identified alcohol with sperm).

In the case of her husband, whom she did not love, the patient found this repulsive and therefore retreated and masturbated.

In this way, “metaphysics” is the cause for masturbation and also becomes the cause of its consequences, of the calcification of bones.

Summary: The question is how the patient could replace masturbation (autoerotic isolation) with positive love towards a man, because lack of money and lack of love have the same meaning for her.

This complex shows variations, particularly, in the following symbols: The bowels of the poor become disinfected; various spoiled (poor and impure) objects are associated with gold and other objects of wealth.

Coitus is expressed through purification, but also through killing, boiling out, burning, and alcoholizing.

Sperm at times means ash, other times powder, or disinfectant.

The uterus sometimes means bowels, at other times, glass, etc. It is characteristic that at first a doubled sexual act (“burning” and “disinfecting”) results from negating sexuality.

This symbolism is repeated time and again, for example, through terms like “washed,” “purified,” “burnt,” “alcoholized,” etc.

A Case of Schizophrenia  47 5.

Poetry of the tropics and water symbolism The patient claims that when she was twelve to thirteen years old, she knew a young painter, and she recounts the following: He was a mythologist because he could bring back to life that which was dead.

His science was always closed off; it has to do with Segantini and palm trees.

Once in his dream, he saw wonderful forests with marvelous women, magnificent fantasies, to which he tried to give immortality by painting them on the stones in a quarry.

Already back then, he was God’s favorite.

His mother was a well-established resident of Bern, who loved painted porcelain.

He was quiet, calm, and lonely.

When his mother died, he cried for her.

The artist, whose personality, evidently, quite appeals to the patient, is the prototype of Professor Forel, whom she also claimed was able to animate stones and possessed a great “sculptural mind.” The patient herself is the stone to which the Professor gives life.

In a similar fashion, this is probably also true for the painter.

Furthermore, the patient says: The painter was said to not be in his right mind because he was searching for his ideals in art.

I only knew him more closely for fourteen days and concluded that he could give art a new direction; perhaps it would be the art of the tropics.

He told me about Fata Morgana.

I am to be envied that I was allowed to see so much of my nature.

During my childhood games, I often had hallucinations about the tropics, as if I was permitted to get a glimpse of a country that no one else had ever seen before.

Back then, I was still unaware of what mythology56 was.

The patient understands “Fata Morgana” also as a mirage that to her, as we know, represents reality. 57  At the same time, a mirage is a phenomenon in hot countries, which partially might have inspired her fantasies of the tropics. “Laocoön,”58 she claims, “is the sphinx which could explain the poetry of the tropics: Perhaps it is a forest with palm trees, cozy places, and good animals who are not frightening, animals nourished by genesis.”

48  A Case of Schizophrenia Question: “Why so?” Answer: “It means genesis of the human fetus, it means sacrificed children.

It can be the birth of a half-grown being, a fetus, or the sacrifice of a mother to save the father.

In all of this, the mother would appear to be a barbarian, if she threw a child to the animal.

These are mission dangers.

One sacrifices the children so that the animals get caught.” The symbol of the creation of a new human being, Laocoön, could explain the poetry of the tropics; that is, that this poetry59 has to do with the genesis of humans. “The animals are nourished by the genesis of the human fetus.” By this, the patient wants to express that animals contain seeds of the human being that the patient had lost during her spontaneous abortion60 and that the animals ate.

The patient describes the throwing of the child to the animals a “sacrifice of the mother in order to save the father.” “If it is only physical duty, not love, then it is just a sacrifice,” says the patient about the sexual relationship with her husband whom she does not love and also blames for her disease and the spontaneous abortion. 61  Thus she sacrifices her child to the father in order to save him or rather, since in her mind saving means “treating” (= having coitus), she loses her child when she has coitus with the man she does not love.

However, since ideas of childbirth are associated with coitus, she uses this opportunity to turn her misfortune into a wish fulfillment.

She does not simply let her child disappear, but brings him back into the father (animal), so that the animal “nourished by genesis” becomes procreative again.

The sacrifice is also called “mission danger.” Mission to the patient encompasses the “conversion of heathens to Christianity.” Heathens are disbelievers, Christians are believers. “Religion,” faith, as the opposite to the animalistic sexual, is, as has been illustrated numerous times, a symbol of the animalistic: “Conversion to Christianity” means the same as “conversion to sexuality.”62 The patient continues: Imagine a woman in a shipwreck is pregnant, and the husband is perhaps a doctor and sacrifices the child in order to save the wife.

What if he is happy that the woman is gone?

Then he throws her to the animals.

What if the woman knows that her husband likes to live?

Then she throws herself to the animals.

These are mission dangers that I have to experience because I am a mission experiment.

I have encountered this danger, when sea animals who needed food pursued

A Case of Schizophrenia  49 the ships, and the woman was willing to sacrifice her child.

There I had many visions that my children were sacrificed to the animals.

Question: “How are the children sacrificed to the animals?” Answer: “They are sacrificed with me for the mission.” The sentence “If the husband is a doctor” is noteworthy.

Sure enough, probably the doctor sacrificed her child (fetus) during her spontaneous abortion.

This gives cause to compare the behavior of her husband, who is indirectly to blame for the spontaneous abortion, to the action of the doctor who actively removes the child.

From this comparison the patient, as she always does, creates an identification: Instead of saying, “if the husband, like the doctor . . . sacrificed the child in order to save me,” she says, “if the husband is a doctor and sacrifices the child in order to save his wife.” The identification is helped by the double meaning of the word “to save” which, as is well known, equals “to treat” which means to have coitus.

Now we also understand why the “salvation” on the part of the doctor is contrasted with “What if her husband is happy that the woman is gone?” Her husband did not want to “save” (that is, “have sexual relations with”) her, like the doctor; after all, he preferred That Woman over her!

However, the word “child,” too, receives a different meaning.

For what does a husband sacrifice to his wife when he wants to have coitus with her?

The same thing that a woman also sacrifices: She throws herself with her children to the animals.

Earlier, we heard that animals ate “children,” and we interpreted it as coitus in which the “child” assumes the role of a sexual product.

That was a sacrifice.

At my question as to how the children are sacrificed, the patient answers in this way: “They are sacrificed with me for the mission.”63 Through this action, the “child” becomes, even more so, an inseparable part of his mother; in a sense, her sexual organ.

What, however, does “shipwreck” mean?

The patient recounts that she had two premature births: “It was a shipwreck, a ship cabin wreck.” Question: “What do you mean by ship cabin wreck?” Answer: “The ship cabin wreck happens if, as part of a divine judgment, one is surrounded by the animals.

I was in a cell, in a J-cell,64 where I was covered with a square blanket; there was a snake.

It constantly appeared and then retreated.

The snake may have a human mind,65 may be a divine judgment; it is a friend of children.

It would save those children who are necessary to preserve human life.”

50  A Case of Schizophrenia (After these words the patient lies down.) The serpent is a judgment of God, therefore a divine judgment.

(The meaning of the judgment, of the punishment, is already known.)66 The serpent saves those children who are necessary to preserve human life. “To save” = to copulate.

Therefore, the serpent copulates with children, in order to preserve the human species.

This confirms that the “child” is a symbol for her sexual organ.

Question: “How does the snake save?” Answer: “It can be useful, but it can also give poison that kills.” She thinks of the magnificent colors of the serpent: It is an animal of God that has most wonderful colors: green, blue, and white.

The rattlesnake is green;67 it is quite dangerous, twines around the human being and crushes it.

This reminds me of circus and menagerie experiments.

The snake is the symbol of deceitfulness.

On the pretext of saving me and not biting me, it crawled on me.

Perhaps it is the symbol of mythology. 68  Mythology has to do with the animals that come about through water and fire, various animals of the ocean.

From these, different animals develop.

Immediately after this, the patient addresses what was analyzed in chapter 2, “Psychological-Sistine experiments,” and states: “A human being can also be dissolved in wine.” Here I must refer to former arguments concerning this point, where we saw that the human being dissolved in wine signifies the fetus in the mother’s womb, and the water is the “water saturated with childlikeness.” We can find further examples with corresponding water fantasies; for example, we will still hear about “spermatic baths,” etc. One could point out again and again how the positive is expressed in the negative.

Thus, for example, the serpent becomes useful through its poisonous bite.

The serpent is the “symbol of mythology,” that is, of the genesis of the human fetus.

Undoubtedly, the poison represents the sperm.

What other “poison” could one otherwise expect from the symbol of the genesis of the human fetus?

The term “poison” should not surprise us since we already heard that the spermatic material is a “dead substance.” The snake “saves” the patient by impregnating her.

The serpent, or perhaps other animals, “eat the ship’s

A Case of Schizophrenia  51 victims in the water”; that is, her children in her womb, or rather in the spermatic water.

In this way, new animals are created.

The act of burgeoning life is represented with death symbolism; that is, the pregnancies that ended in spontaneous abortions find compensation in an unreal (negative-symbolic) restoration of the pregnancy.

We also have other examples for this mechanism.

For instance, often during the analysis we have evidence of her antagonistic attitude towards her sister: The sister wants to be her sole heir; the sister joins in the dirty assumptions of That Woman, etc. The patient describes her sister as floating in a basket like Moses on the upper Lake Zurich.

To the question of what this means, she promptly answers that it means danger.

She then claims that she saw her sister at home suffering from a weak heart.

As Rank69 showed, the Moses basket is the womb.

The patient’s idea confirms this.

Like the heroes in Rank’s thinking and like the child (fetus) in the patient’s earlier view, the sister, too, is eliminated by being placed back into the mother’s womb, presumably to be born again.

It is quite likely that for the patient, the sister fulfills a dual task by also becoming a sexual symbol, just like the “child,” as shown above, also becomes a sexual symbol.

The upper Lake Zurich is the place where the patient experienced her first erotic desire, and it is at this place she has her sister perish.

The next dream would also support this interpretation: The patient sees herself wade in unclean water across the whole of Lake Zurich.

In this context, she recalls: The sister was connected to Professor Forel’s younger brother in school, in a school-path-poetry.

He wanted to prostitute her, but I said to her: Push him away from you!

Artists have rather permissive attitudes!

Of course, the “school-path-poetry” does not really exist but is a fantasy. “Professor Forel’s brother,” also an “artist,” is Dr. J., (perhaps the word “younger” already points to this.) Dr. J. is, on one hand, an instructor as her psychiatrist; on the other hand, his name is Karl, and he is tall.

In this way, he reminds her of Karl der Grosse [Charlemagne] and his school reforms.

Likewise, the patient has chains of associations between Dr. J. and Charlemagne.

One should also keep in mind that her husband, a professor, is often identified with the doctor, so that her husband’s profession is turned into that of the doctor, and vice versa.

52  A Case of Schizophrenia Thus her expression “school-path-poetry.” The patient has many fantasies in which her wish to be “prostituted” by Dr. J. comes true.

In this instance, the patient’s sister assumes the role that, in fact, the patient’s sexuality would like to play.

In the patient’s dream the impure water corresponds to Dr. J.’s “dirty” (impure) desire with respect to her sister. 70  “The souls that fell into the water,” according to the patient, “are saved by God.

They fall onto deeper ground.

I was pulled into the water by my hair while bathing.

The souls are rescued by the Sun God.” Now we indeed see that the “souls that fell into the water” are “saved.” Therefore, death simply means rebirth.

Immediately thereafter, the patient imagines hearing a voice: “Near the Monastery of Wurmspach, young girls were riding on a ship.

The ship had a leak, and they did not believe in God and Jesus Christ and, therefore, had to die.”71 We know that the patient calls her spontaneous abortion a “shipwreck”: “It was a shipwreck, a ship cabin wreck,” she mentioned earlier.

At that moment, too, she thinks of a shipwreck to which “godless” girls fell “victim.” The voice also reminds her of “Catholic consequences,” that is, of consequences that result from bad moral conduct of the Catholics (her husband).

The patient blames her husband’s infidelity for her spontaneous abortion.

Furthermore, the voice reminds her of a ride she had taken a few days before she heard about the misfortune.

The patient claims that she lost a medallion with the photograph of her sister and a stone with seven pearls at the exact same location where the above-mentioned accident occurred.

Just as the victims of the shipwreck and the patient and her children were “spilled”72 into the water, and just as the sister was placed into the water in a basket like Moses, so too the medallion with the photograph of her sister and the stone were lost. 73  These are all symbols relating to the “spillage” of the products of the spontaneous abortion that, as shown above, are returned to their point of origin (water-womb), in order to be born again.

Summary: In this chapter, we discussed the abortus complex.

As always, in this chapter, too, death signifies a “resurrection.”74 In Rank’s thinking, the destruction of the fetus is represented as a return into the parents (in his thinking, the mother womb), from where a rebirth takes place.

The patient perceives this return as a sexual act.

(The “victims” are eaten by animals.) The fetus (child) obtains the meaning of the sexual organ. 75  This

A Case of Schizophrenia  53 identification of sexual organ and child should not seem strange to us.

We know of many examples from language usage where the creator is identified by that which he creates or by his procreating organ.

For instance, in the language of wet nurses and children, the Russian word for Papa – the father – means also “to eat” or “bread” (which the father provides).

Likewise, “niania” means “the nanny,” and “niamniam” “to eat.” “Mama” is the name for “the mother,” and “mamma” the name for “the breast organ.” A parallel to this is “mother,” meaning “uterus” [Gebärmutter].

In Russian, there is the word “matka,” which means “mother,” but also “uterus.” These are all examples that are common knowledge.

It is therefore incomprehensible why critics get worked up about Stekel’s statement that in dreams relatives can also represent the genitals. 6.

Iron, fire, war The patient says: “There are non-arbitrary and arbitrary iron products.

The arbitrary products are gained from a smith’s hearth.

One can add them to coffee, but they have to be used in a very small amount, so that the essence that develops can be dissolved.

They have to be chemically pure, a kind of Novozoon, a powder that is formed from a sort of hydrogen.” In the chapter “Psychological-Sistine experiments,” we encountered Novozoon understood as sperm.

There, too, the patient claims “Novozoon” was “made from a kind of hydrogen.” Thus the chemically pure iron and sperm (Novozoon) represent the same.

For this reason, a new being (human being) evolves from it as well.

We have already learned that a human being can be dissolved in water (in the “spermatic water of Jesus, saturated with blood”).

Here, the iron powder, that is, the sperm, is dissolved in coffee.

We heard about coffee in the chapter “Histology and its treatment,” and first assumed that coffee would correspond to blood.

Here the same interpretation suggests itself to us: The powder dissolved in coffee is the human being dissolved in blood.

The patient imagines that in the mother’s womb the human being is present, dissolved in blood. 76  As was noted in the chapter “Industrial question,” the patient’s attention was drawn to iron when thinking of her husband’s “overpowering” nature. “If one has too much iron in one’s body, one becomes overpowering: After all, people use the expression ‘iron constitution’.” Being an “alcoholic,” her husband was “overpowering.” We already heard that being overpowered leads to

54  A Case of Schizophrenia masturbation, which, because it causes illness of the sex organs, leads to a lack of breast milk production.

Since artificial milk contains a lot of calcium, from “being overpowered,” “metaphysical calcification of the bones” occurs.

By “metaphysical” the patient means “overpowering.” We also heard that the bones are “purified” through coitus.

Hence, we can understand the following sentence: “When too many iron additives77 for the purification of the bones are present in the body, metaphysical illness is the result” (that is, the illness which comes from being overpowered, or rather, from metaphysics).

With the expression “being overpowered,” the patient refers to her husband’s increased sexual libido that she found disgusting.

For that reason, she takes refuge in the more refined vegetarian remedies (rejection of the animalistic). “More delicate specimens,” she continues, “would be hazelnuts, almonds, cherries, plum seeds, more delicate vegetables, more delicate fibre formations and cloth fibre formations . . .,” etc. Furthermore, she talks about iron again: “Geologists have brought stone in contact with iron.

That creates fire.

The hot stone can heat the iron, or vice versa.

When the iron is hot, one can forge it.

This has to do with the new creation of a human being.” The “forging” is an analogy to “sculptural art.” The comment that follows corresponds to this: “This can be brought about by pathological science and the mythological science.” The patient uses the term “science” in terms of illness, as was shown in the chapter “Histology, etc.,” where the illness denotes a sexual disease, or rather, sexual excessiveness.

This excessiveness can be pathological (illness-inducing), but it can also be mythological; that is, it can have to do with the genesis of humans.

The pathological science is the human dust and has to do with sculptural art; he himself78 dedicated sculptural art to the cemetery.

The dead then need to be raised again.

When the souls have risen high, they die in Jesus Christ.

However, when death comes and Jesus Christ is at the bed of the dying, there is no pain: He saves the souls from the valley of the shadow of death and takes them into a different kingdom.

The dust has to serve man for the creation of a new human being: a new absorption of substance by the painted stone, the embodiment of Vehmic art which wanted to evoke the pathological one.

Through “Vehmic art” (masturbation), the patient became ill and turned into a “dead stone” (“the Vehmic art wanted to evoke the pathological

A Case of Schizophrenia  55 one”), but it is the dead from which new life comes. 79  Vehmic art, by killing, creates new life.

This view is also in line with the Christian theory of salvation; namely, that those who die in Christ are born into eternal life.

She continues: One needs the iron for the purpose of penetrating the earth, for the purpose of a fiery ending.

With the iron one can create cold human beings from stone.

Those humans who unjustly suffer from being locked up must be saved.

In the case of humans, it is the teaching of anatomy: The earth is split and blasted, and the human being is divided.

Surgery is aware of this.

The human being is split apart and put back together again.

Here, the patient imagines iron as a piece of iron that is used for the penetration of the earth, that is, the woman.

She arrives at such fantasies after she has talked about the creation of a new human being. “In order to put an end to being buried alive,” the patient adds, “Jesus Christ asked his disciples to penetrate the earth.

I was freed from the valley of the shadow of death through Professor Forel.”80 What follows are the above-mentioned shipwreck fantasies that belong to the abortus complex.

It goes without saying that the penetration of the earth refers to the impregnation of a woman.

We already know that the patient modifies the operation of the “mother” by Professor Kocher into a symbol for the sexual act (cf. “Professor Kocher wanted to force me to have sexual pleasure,” and the explanations in that context).

It is, therefore, comprehensible that the mention of surgery serves as a reference to the sexual act: “Surgery knows this.” The redemption of humans who suffer from being locked up (like the patient who is locked up in the institution), is “the teaching of anatomy.” Just as in the chapter “Histology, etc.” “science of the tissues” was called “illness,” here the patient uses, vice versa, “teaching” for “illness.” In the language of the patient, one would have to rephrase the sentence to the following: “It is an illness that has to do with the female anatomy.” Indeed, shortly after, she talks about her spontaneous abortion.

The associations of the splitting of the earth correspond to the ideas about birth: The woman (earth) is being “split”; that is, a crevice is formed through which the child is coming out.

In the chapter “PsychologicalSistine experiments” we observed the same representation of birth: “It is a description of the Italian lakes; they become visible through a chasm in

56  A Case of Schizophrenia the earth” (body of the woman).

This process led to the creation of legends that deal with the genesis of humans.

However, in the patient’s thinking, legend and dream alike represent reality.

Therefore, one could simply say: “They are Italian lakes,” etc. “This has to do with the genesis of humans.” We are also familiar with the “anatomic examination” as the “sectioning of the soul” that Dr. J. conducts on his patient and which turned out to be a sexual treatment.

In the following section, we encounter the same mechanism: Mr. S., owner of the iron fire control in Russia, has an association with another factory owner whose daughter was not nice to me; she was somewhat naughty: When I was in the J,81 she came there as a student and partly vaccinated, partly punctured me.

The result was open wounds that turned into abscesses.

I asked her what a lindworm was.

The young woman showed me her tongue, then she said: ‘If you had once lived in good conditions, I would be politer towards you.’ I met the woman in the institution.

Her name was Miss ‘Goldenb . . . ,’ she had lovely golden-brown hair and a delicate body.

Mr. S. sometimes told me about her.

Mr. S. was my husband’s friend.

He was quite intelligent and had a comfortable demeanor.

He and his wife found me likeable.

Mr. S. was sick for a long time.

Turning towards me, she says: “Do you know what a lindworm is?” Judging from the above, it follows that the patient liked the factory owner S., whether as a person or as a symbol for fire control, the latter of which – as I will elaborate later, is a consistent sexual symbol.

Be that as it may, the fact is, his partner’s daughter, a person who has a close relationship to him, gives the patient a puncture or vaccination. 82  The “daughter” is a Russian student. 83  This can be considered an analogy to me, and also corresponds to the fact that she asks me the same question that she asked that lady.

The “daughter” is naughty, yet still likeable to the patient, because the latter finds her quite beautiful.

The patient showed this positive transference also towards me, since she frequently made me compliments, and even wanted to kiss me.

Asking questions about something embarrassing, like the “lindworm,” is exhibitionism through words.

Dr. J., too, first “examined” the patient and then performed the (sexual) “function” on her.

The patient shows me her difficulties.

She expects that I could control

A Case of Schizophrenia  57 her “sexual dysentery,” by providing her with what she desires (that is, the man).

Since she transfers the pertaining fantasies onto me, I instantly become a “sexual person.” She tells me: You, as a doctor, have to take charge of controlling the dysentery.

This has to do with Marmite.

You have scarlet fever, and you must be careful not to get dysentery.

You can control dysentery through geological-vegetarian-mythological forest therapeutics.

(It is the) Liebig mineral theory.

It is the composition of the blood which, depending on its nature, becomes more liquid or more solid.

Afterwards, the patient talks about the “Kocher lymph,” etc., that was already discussed earlier (lymph = sperm).

According to the patient, I myself (the consultant) am “infected,” suffer from “scarlet fever,” and could get “dysentery,” just like anyone else to whom the patient has “transferred” in a positive or negative way.

Everyone needs to be saved.

To achieve this goal, complicated “therapeutics” must intervene, indeed “geological” ones, since it is “geology” that connects stone with iron (for the creation of a new human being); “vegetarian” ones, because in the anti-sexual the sexual is concealed at its most intense; finally, “mythological” ones, which clearly means that it “has to do with the creation of a new human being.” “Forest therapeutics” – because “animals nourished by genesis” live in the forest. 84  By coagulation of the blood, the patient most likely refers to pregnancy.

It is a folk superstition to believe that menstrual blood is used in the formation of a child: The blood no longer flows and thickens, and the child’s body is formed from it.

Right after thinking of the penetration of the earth, the patient thinks of the factory owner S. and, specifically, the female student who also “penetrated” her since she “vaccinated” or “punctured” her.

There, too, we may interpret penetration as fertilization. 85  An abscess develops, that is, a tumour, which alludes to the swelling of the uterus.

The fact that the “abscess” is a sign of disease is not a contradiction since, in the patient’s mind, the entire process is inextricably mixed with ideas about disease.

We will now turn to the darker question: “What is the lindworm?” The patient instructs me:

58  A Case of Schizophrenia The lindworm is larger than the room.

It lives in the ocean and snaps up animals.

It is like a divine judgment.

I saw this animal, with my brother on it, protected by a lion.

My brother sat in the Russian part of Poland at the border of an ocean in a park-like forest.

The animal symbolized a kind of judgment that would sign the European peace.

One should know that the patient employs an abundance of war symbols when expressing her clashes with her surroundings and her severe sufferings.

For example, during anesthesia, when she had the spontaneous abortion, she had a dream about the Russo-Japanese War.

She had her sufferings represented by soldiers whom she saw wounded and in miserable condition, and for whom she felt pity.

To her, war is a collective term for “to kill,” “to wound,” etc.; furthermore, it has the same masochistic = sexual coloring as any other torture, and demands the same “redemption” = treatment.

The same is true for the opposite of war, “peace,”86 which, for practical purposes, is also brought about through a kind of “divine judgment.” We have encountered the exact same expression in the case of the “serpent.” After all, the lindworm is a giant serpent that also “saves” in exactly the same manner.

On the serpent sits the brother.

Freud87 pointed out that children represent the possession of something by sitting on it.

Here it would mean that the brother is the owner of the “lindworm” and, therefore, the person who makes “peace.” If this assumption is correct, we will have to be able to prove a positive transference to the brother.

This is indeed possible, if we recall that the active person is called “brother.” For example, Dr. J.: brother of Professor Forel; furthermore, brother of Professor Kocher.

We will find additional clues for this in chapter 7.

Specifically, with respect to the forest symbolism (the brother sits in a park-like forest), I want to take Riklin’s work into account88 and mention that in the patient’s thinking, God, as in the case of the piece of iron, also “penetrates the earth (= woman) with a ray.” We will find this ray symbolism in other parts as well.

The ray turns out to have the same sexual meaning as the piece of iron.

Since the patient also claims that God sends his rays into the forest, would it not be conceivable that the forest must be understood in Riklin’s sense? 89  With regard to the war symbolism, I asked the patient whether she experienced the war.

The good Lord did this.

When God wants to draw the soul of a child to himself, then no force can prevent it.

The patient is “suffering from lung disease and syphilis,” due to her bad lifestyle, as we have learned.

The fact that the good Lord through his shot caused her to suffer from lung disease (which in her case equals suffering from syphilis) means that he “prostituted” her.

In my opinion, this conclusion can be drawn without difficulties, since we already learned how the good Lord “saves” her with his “spermatic water” and, furthermore, how he “punishes” her.

She also claims that Dr. J.

(analogue of Jesus Christ) had “prostituted” her, that he was a Mormon friend who wanted to have a divorce every year. 90  A little later, the patient denies that God shot at her, rather, that they were shots from the war.

Her denial merely shows the stronger emphasis on emotions and the insecurity typical for comments about a complex.

Let us recall how in the chapter “Psychological-Sistine experiments,” the patient is reluctant to include Dr. J. among alcoholics. “I would not know whether this has anything to do with Dr. J.” Let’s listen further to what the patient says: I was once shot through my head, one time through the chest, and one time through the eyes.

Then a resurrection of only the spirit took place, perhaps through Dr. J., through the mission, in the mythological mission question of Catholic filiation.

Here Christ’s role is assumed by Dr. J., who enables the patient to be resurrected – by being shot three times.

60  A Case of Schizophrenia having coitus.

Jesus said: “Let the children come to me, and do not hold them back.”92 The “mission” (mission question) is about the “question of filiation”; that is, about the creation = the begetting of children, because the latter consists of the examination93 of the “religious question” = the sexual question.

As we know, the “examination” is followed by performing the corresponding “function”; that is, the coitus that leads to making children.

Question: “What does this have to do with Dr. J.?” Answer: “He said that his father was a minister and that his schooling was pure; it is an upbringing that aims at lifting up a nation, that is, those who deserve it, to a higher level.” Dr. J. is indeed the son of a minister.

The patient views his “purity” in that he prefers the poor (the “[common] people”), to whom the patient belongs, in contrast to her “impure” husband who preferred a rich girl over her.

Question: “Why a shot through the eyes?” Answer: “In order to dedicate the inner eye to God, for the resurrection of the spirits that possess pure intention.
